## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The governing equation follows Newton's second law with nonlinear restoring forces, possible damping, and possible driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force with linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic nonlinearity with damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic driving force)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven cubic oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (combined quadratic and cubic terms)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x (position-dependent damping)
- Coulomb-type friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v) (quadratic damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- General driven nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (full Duffing with phase)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium â€” expect symmetric potentials
- Even-power terms (x**2) break oscillation symmetry â€” indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection
- Products of x**2 * v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type), causing limit cycle behavior
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (no explicit t), the system is autonomous and energy methods apply
- Cubic terms x**3 with sign opposite to linear term x indicate hardening/softening spring behavior
- Absence of velocity terms indicates a conservative (energy-preserving) system
- Products x*v suggest velocity-position coupling typical of nonlinear friction or Rayleigh dissipation
- Multiple frequency components in time suggest quasi-periodic or parametrically driven systems
